function imgOn(imgName) {
if (document.images) {
 document[imgName].src = eval(imgName + "on.src");
 }
}

function imgOff(imgName) {
if (document.images) {
 document[imgName].src = eval(imgName + "off.src");
 }
}

           <td valign="top" width="50%">
            <hr width="90%"/>
            <font color="#e0e0e0" face="arial">
             <b>
              2010
              <a href="images/press.html" title="Click here for more information">
               AAS Chambliss Amateur Achievement Award
              </a>
              Recipient
             </b>
            </font>
            <hr width="90%"/>
            <br/>
            <font face="arial" size="-1">
             <b>
              Presenting images of interesting astronomical subjects
             </b>
             obtained with modest, commercially available
             <a href="#telescopes">
              telescopes
             </a>
             and CCD
             <a href="http://www.sbig.com" rel="nofollow" target="top">
              cameras
             </a>
             that are optimized for taking long exposures of low light-level subjects.  Separate black and white exposures through clear, red, green and blue filters are digitally combined and stretched, using Adobe Photoshop and other image processing software, to create full color pictures.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             <b>
              Earlier images, near the page bottom, were exposed from suburban, San Jose, California
             </b>
             <a href="images/night_scenes.html">
              location
             </a>
             through moderately high light pollution with a 12-inch
             <a href="images/mewlon.html">
              Dall-Kirkham
             </a>
             cassegrain telescope.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             <b>
              Most images were produced
             </b>
             through the remotely controlled
             <a href="images/rc.html">
              half-meter
             </a>
             Ritchey-Chretien telescope at the Blackbird Observatory.  Some southern hemisphere images were also acquired from a remotely operated observatory located near Melbourne,
             <a href="images/southern_astro.html">
              Australia
             </a>
             with a 12-inch RCOS telescope.  A few pictures, noted as
             <a href="images/noao.html">
              NOAO
             </a>
             , were acquired with the 20-inch Ritchey-Chretien telescope at the National Optical Astronomy Observatory Visitors Center on Kitt Peak, Arizona.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Please
             <a href="mailto:rj2010@cosmotography.com">
              contact
             </a>
             me anytime with comments or questions.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             <b>
              All images and written content are copyright ©2004- 2018 by R Jay GaBany
             </b>
             . Please do not reproduce or distribute without permission.
            </font>
           </td>
